Rememoried is a first-person adventure game, focused on the ideas of dreams and memories with surrealistic, explorative and puzzle-solving settings.

The way you advance in the game is by looking away from your surroundings, elements in the environment, and other important objects for they‚Äôll constantly change shape and create a new path.

‚ÄúYou count the stars above your head just like the one who pointed a finger at you from the unknown. The closer you get to infinity, the more you get lost in the numbers created to describe the real world, and your eyelids become curtains that hide unexpected discoveries beyond the borders, reached by only the strongest thoughts. This exciting play for one spectator is a reward for everyday gifts of the mind.‚Äù

The game is visually stunning, along the sound of flowing water combined with the elegant classical and eerie electronic music.

Non recommand√©
2.8 h en tout
√âvaluation publi√©e le 21 novembre 2015
I absolutely love games that are often described as "walking simulators" (Dear Esther, The Path, etc.), as what they lack in gameplay they generally make up for in story, dialogue, and visuals. Unfortunately, Rememoried is lacking in almost every aspect.

The art style, while nice and minimalist, sometimes makes it hard to see where you're supposed to be going next. This is especially frustrating during the vertical portions of the game. The dialogue is atrocious, vague, and the sound design leans way too heavy on the reverb. If subtitles weren't present I wouldn't be able to decipher much of what's said. Most importantly, Rememoried is much less a walking simulator than it is a "stepping stones" simulator.

There is so much emphasis placed on platforming in this game when the controls are too sluggish to offer any real precision. I'd often become quite frustrated after having spent so long trying to jump across a seemingly endless amount of rotating cogs or floating boulders, only to fall off near the end, having to start over again several times.

Rememoried is a promising game, I really do enjoy the glitchy visuals and the premise of being trapped in the protagonist's dream but I feel that the developer let its potential go to waste and, rather than focus on a story-driven adventure game, instead opted for yet another platformer type adventure game with a unique art style.

Despite the cringeworthy dialogue, I started out quite impressed and quickly found myself not being able to enjoy Rememoried at all.

Rememoried is a decent enough game with some smart ideas that shoots itself in the foot with shoddy gameplay, which is always frustrating to witness.

The main gameplay mechanic is the ability to ‚Äòrememory‚Äô objects (mainly platforms) by looking away, meaning the world changes when it is not observed. That‚Äôs a good idea, but it doesn‚Äôt make a good game alone. Despite being compared to and tagged as a walking simulator, Rememoried is actually a confused puzzle platformer, where you spend half your time stuck on levels whose solution doesn‚Äôt make a lick of sense (BECAUSE SURREALISM!) and the other half on drawn out, poorly-designed platforming levels where the camera, the jumping mechanics and the hypercontrasted graphics all conspire to make you fall to your death for the umpteenth time in a row.

But maybe the point of the game is the story!‚Ä¶except there is none. And i don‚Äôt mean ¬´ the story is confusing or barely hinted at ¬ª. I mean there are approximately two lines of trite ¬´ spoken word ¬ª per level (all of which i‚Äôve heard about as many times as i restarted the levels, i.e. way too much), and they aren‚Äôt exactly mindblowing (¬´ Logic is a dogma. ¬ª HOW PROFOUND.). Admittedly, the game is definitely surrealist in its lack of a defined narrative and its interest with dreams and how they shape memories, but here‚Äôs the thing: this kind of contemplation simply doesn‚Äôt fit in a game burdened with sloppy gameplay. There is nothing dreamlike or surrealist about the mechanics of the game and to me, that‚Äôs why it fails completely.

I truly wish Rememoried were an actual walking simulator, because it has a great soundtrack, a beautiful aesthetic and some truly captivating moments that made me feel like i was experiencing something different and unique to the game. But those are few and far between and I can only recommend this game as an interesting but failed experiment.


As an aside, the description states that failing a level brings the player back to previous levels. As someone who has failed every level it was possible to fail, I can say pretty confidently that this is not the case anymore. Don‚Äôt get me wrong, THANK GOD FOR THAT, but it‚Äôs something you might want to take into account.

√âvaluation publi√©e le 27 d√©cembre 2015
Summary:
Rememoried is a short adventure puzzle game about exploring the surreal world of dreams and memories. You might think this is just another walking simulator without any proper gameplay but you'd be wrong - the game is focused on puzzles and platforming.

All puzzles are based on moving or jumping, there aren't any items to pickup or interact with. You just have to wander through the levels and find the way out. Many environmental elements are usually not stable and (almost) every time you stop looking at a platforms (clouds, for example), they change their positions.

Rememoried isn't just about the gameplay, it's really worth praising the graphics and sounds, the whole atmosphere in most levels will make you often stop and just look around to enjoy what developer's artistic skills made.

Pros:
- Well-thought puzzles where you won't get stuck for more than few minutes.
- The world around you changes almost everytime you look to another direction (in levels focused on platforming).
- Great atmosphere. The surreal world of Rememoried is beautiful.
- Nice soundtrack.

‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•:
- Short length. Expect getting 100% achievements after 3 hours of gameplay.



Disclaimer: My copy of Rememoried was obtained for free - I won the game in a giveaway that might have been sponsored by the developer. This fact hasn't changed my opinion about the game (and the review) in any way.
 
Samm

√âvaluation publi√©e le 22 septembre 2015
PLEASE DO NOT PLAY THIS GAME.

Dont get me wrong: This is one of the most gorgeous games I have ever had the chance to see, and it was a real treat for a while that made it absolutely terrific. And then suddenly? It becomes more rage inducing than any game I have ever played in my life.

This game is essentially pretty precision platformer: the game. The main gameplay mechanic is to basically spin around in a circle over and over to make objects magically move positions in a system the game likes to call "forgetting". This ends up being a horrible platformer where you need to spin around in circles to make a platform appear close enough to you so you can land on it, and then spin around some more to make another one get closer to you. Some parts of the game aren't like this, are much more straightforward, and honestly fairly enjoyable. But at one point in the game I just could not take it anymore. The platforms were too small, nearly impossible to see in the dark, and I kept falling off of them because they were literally spheres. It was total baloney.

Once again, do not get this game. Please watch a dedicated and skilled Let's Player play through the game for you so you have the chance to see how pretty the game can really be. Do not buy this game thinking it will be some zen experience worthwhile of your time. The developers wanted it to be zen-like, to be taken slowly, but allow me to tell you that when you're stuck in one area for far too long, it is not worth that "zen-like" feeling.

3/10, pretty graphics and cinematography at least. This was a game designed by a brilliant artist...but not a brilliant game designer.
 
Luc Ienn

√âvaluation publi√©e le 15 septembre 2015
Confusing at first, but eventually becomes a really unique and intruiging puzzle game that relies more on intuition than anything else for you to "solve" the puzzle. Very rewarding puzzle solving as well as quite an immersive experience.

Can be a little frustrating but is pretty different enough from other puzzle games to stand out.

If your looking for a walking simulator, this isn't really one however. If you want to check out some gameplay before buying, feel free to check out my playthrough.

REMEMORIED | #1 A Dive Into The Surreal! (Let's Play PC Gameplay 60fps)

Non recommand√©
2.3 h en tout
√âvaluation publi√©e le 12 juillet 2017
Beautiful and unique graphics, and incredible concept and atmosphere - but I'm afraid the frustrating gameplay overwhelmed them all for me. The mechanic of "forgetting" means you spend a lot of time spinning in circles, which is not great for motion sickness. This is particularly problematic for the level where you need to jump across turning cogs, whilst spinning around to make new cogs appear. This leads to many frustrating deaths, and it made me so sick I had to quit the game several times. I'm just not sure "atmospheric psychedelic mind-bender" and "frustrating platformer" are two categories that go well together?

It's also often not clear what you need to do - to the point that it can become annoying. I like surrealism and not being spoonfed, but some puzzles I completed without even knowing why or how. I'm not sure if there's meant to be a story or message we are supposed to follow, but the voice over phrases came across as nonsensical and therefore pretentious rather than genuinely deep.

I really wanted to like this, but I feel like it's a bit of a wasted opportunity. I know I've been predominantly negative, but I liked this enough to want to keep an eye out for what the developers create in the future. I really hope they build on the graphics and the atmosphere they've created here and move in a slightly different direction for their next game - hopefully more towards atmospheric exploration than face-palming platformer.
 
loofychan

√âvaluation publi√©e le 4 f√©vrier 2017
The artistic direction of this game (visuals and soul) are beautiful and very well made. I can definitely tell that a lot of work has been put into it. With that said, two things prevent me from recommend it: gameplay and story.

The gameplay, while innovative at first, never really changes its root: Look away from objects to make them change until their disposition becomes useful to you. So, you will spend 95% of your time turning your camera over and over praying that RNG finally places the platforms well enough for a jump. Coupled with the fact that the puzzle solutions make absolutely no sense, it turns from enjoyable to repetitive to annoying to frustrating pretty quickly.

The story, well... I'm not sure there's a story. There's voices talking and saying stuff, but not once I've been able to make sense out of anything they said. Maybe I'm just too stupid for this game, but usually you can at least, upon beating a game, throw a guess about what it all meant - but not here.

On the plus side, the screenshots will make for great wallpapers if you can put up with playing long enough to take them.
 
Drkie

√âvaluation publi√©e le 30 juin 2016
Produit rembours√©

While visually appealing, Rememoried really doesn't deliver much of an experience outside of "Oh, that's pretty!" and even then stops delivering anything different from what you've already seen after the first few puzzles.

The singular mechanic is looking away from the puzzle and then turning back and hoping a new solution has appeared. If not, turn around and see if a new solution has appeared behind you. Repeat until you are able to ascend, or jump stepping stones, or whatever the incredibly vague solution is. At some points, I found myself just spinning slowly in a circle, waiting for rocks to appear to jump on. Of course, this all assumes that you can find some sort of goal in each puzzle of this directionless game.

The dialogue/repetitive background speeches are pretty boring, uninspiring, and a little pretentious, acting as if they're somehow incredibly deep or reflective.

Overall, little to no substance; watch a Let's Play instead.
 
[TM]Nameless

This game baffles me. I'm not sure quite how to feel about it.

It's visually stunning and the music / audio is great. I've completed the game and struggled on at least 3 levels, one being the last level. I'm unsure if I missed a narrative queue here and there, but I got frustrated a bit.

It was a relief to finish it, and I ended up going back again and doing some of the levels again.

Would I recommend it? I'm voting yes...however, I like the 'odd' type of game, so it fits with who I am as a gamer. It may not be for everyone, but if you're up for a unique experience, give it a whirl.

Hmm, i think, i will call it a project, not a game :) It fits better. This project is really peaceful. You don't need drugs or anything like that to complete this game. Imagination and concentration. √âvaluation publi√©e le 27 janvier 2019
This is unquestionably one of the best-looking games I have ever played. Ever since I was a kid, I've been dreaming of being able to experience spaces like this. Rememoried provided surreal environments that are more gorgeous than I could have imagined.

It's quite flawed, however. Unfortunately, it seems that this game suffers from being gamified. Providing a challenge in these landscapes breaks immersion if one falls and restarts the scene. Although some of the levels work fine like this (the star cubes, for example), most of the time, it's an exercise in frustration. I really believe that this game would be one of my favourites if the player was given more forgiving jumps (lower gravity), that would make Rememoried more of a beautiful experience rather than a platformer with tedious traversal.

However, not enough can be said about how great this looks. I accidently restarted the game near the end a couple years ago, causing me to lose all my progress. I waited until I acquired a computer that could run it well, and I have to say the wait was worth it. Although redoing this was devoid of surprise, the knowledge of what to do made my second playthrough smoother, allowing me to enjoy the scenery even more. I will always treasure this game, and plan to play it every so often.
 
quasiotter

√âvaluation publi√©e le 31 octobre 2016
This game is not for everyone, but I would recommend it to anyone. I can see where the mixed reviews have come from because the game does drop you in with no explanation as to what you're doing or how things work, but the puzzles are some of the most innovative mind benders I have experienced. This game teaches you not to trust your senses. Don't trust your instincts. Look away and things change. This game teaches you that forgetting what was behind and what is ahead is the path to enlightenment. If you want puzzles that will have you kicking yourself for not seeing the answer for half an hour when it was right in front of your face, this is one game that gives you that. The graphics are beautiful, the story is confusing, and I walked away from the game with a lot of questions, but also an experience that stuck in my head for the next couple of days.

√âvaluation publi√©e le 31 d√©cembre 2015
I am normally a fan of more abstract games, walking simulators and the like. I usually think of myself as a pretty intuitive person as well. Despite this, I didn't like Rememoried. I played through 2 or 3 levels and it felt more like I was playing a tech demonstration than a game. I didn't understand my character hitbox and how I was going to interact with the geometry in the game. I found it difficult to -jump- on things.

Maybe it was the first person view that tripped me up, but even without that, I didn't feel like I had any idea why I was doing things or going places. I felt punished by "failure" which sometimes was just because I was testing the edge of the level, which then would restart, all voice acting included.

I was excited about this game, but after getting stuck not being able to jump to a platform and having everything else set me back a level, I couldn't keep going.

√âvaluation publi√©e le 7 mars 2016
No. Don't buy it.
The graphics are nicely done, and the basic gameplay idea might be interesting, but overall the experience is poorly designed. For the first three levels it's even interesting to explore some obscure landscapes of procedurally-generated rocks, but then it's just it. The game becomes really frustrating as it goes on, and repeating the same game mechanics just makes it worse. Add some annoying music that loops forever and you get the most stressful game that I have ever played. Maybe it's the intention of the developer, but it would be lame to do so. In my own opinion it's just a bad experiment that has some really good ideas inside. I think just watching the trailer is enough.

√âvaluation publi√©e le 19 d√©cembre 2016
Let me start by saying that I completed the entire game. I enjoyed quite a bit of it and quite a bit frustrated me to the point that I nearly gave up. its been a long time since I last played kikaboo and hide and go seek. That's the mechanism you have to employ to progress in the game. You have to go find something (either a mask, a flower, a mask, a bed, a tree etc etc) and you have to reach it by playing kikaboo. That is because stuff changes when you don't look at it.
I don't know if I should recommend this game or not.....So I am not going to recommend this game.

Let start with all the good stuff:
- It has an amazing soundtrack. Ranging from opera to piano to strange remixes of niel's moon landing speech and it usually fits the theme of the world you are curerntly exploring
- The art is quite beautifull and varied
- Its quite the adventure to explore all these worlds
- unique gameplay mechanics (both a pro and a ‚ô•‚ô•‚ô• since playing kikaboo the entire game will start to get annoying at some point)

And now the bad stuff:
- The game WILL make you dizzy. The theme of this game is that things change as soon as it leaves your field of vision and to progress you'll have to turn around A LOT!!!!
- Everything outside your field of vision and not touching you is subject to change. soooo that means that if you are on a stone floating in mid-air and you jump up the stone can change. Usually when you are on something that is suspended in mid-air you are trying to go up. So if you jump to check if you can jump high enough to make a certain jump you'll suddenly find that the rock below you is at ground level and you have to start all over again. You'll also find that falling down to ground level is a common occurence (at least for me it was). Starting again once or twice is oke. it's annoying but it wouldn't kill the game. starting 8 or 9 time from the very beginning kills the entire mood and leaves you frustrated as hell. restarting 20 times makes you want to quit the game.......
- In some world like the "time" world it is quite easy to fall down. Lets take this "time" world as an example. You'll have to run across ¬±40 cogs that are turning without falling down. Every cog has a hole in the middle that you can fall down though. You'll have to turn around during this run to change the cogs in front of you adding a little extra difficuty. This is a long run and passing from cog to cog is very time consuming. You'll want to hurry and as soon as you move a bit quicker you'll fall down. Now if you fall down you get the standard cutscene of the world spinning. After that is finished you'll get to start ALL OVER AGAIN.......with the same dialog........again and again and again.......it gets really annoying and frustrating and the more frustrating it gets the faster you want to go and the more you'll fall down.....
- SPOILERS!!!!!You have no clue what you are supposed to to to progress in the game. In one world you have to find a little flower without any clues that you are actually looking for a flower. The dialog will talk about other world an you'll see saturn floating in the sky and you'll see lots of stuff but the only significant thing in this world is the little flower near the border END SPOILER!!!!!!

√âvaluation publi√©e le 12 d√©cembre 2015
This is a really tremendous walking sim. It reminds me a bit of Lemma, except (mostly) without parkour. When you first load the game it feels like a pure walking sim in the vein of Proteus because the place is so beautiful and the music is outstanding. It's a delight just to wander about. After a while you start to realize there is some logic in the game and some puzzles to figure out. Most of the puzzles are exploratory, but there are one or two insanely frustrating jumping puzzles that almost had me giving up altogether. Jumping puzzles aside, this is a stunningly gorgeous game with some really cool mechanics and well worth a look for anyone into walking sims or art games.

√âvaluation publi√©e le 2 janvier 2017
This game is a stunning work of art. Everything from the surreal atmosphere to the hauntingly beautiful soundtrack is just superb. The game is rather abstract and it often feels like an out-of-body experience, so, if you're into that sort of philosophical avant garde style, then you'll love it. The imagery is very surreal and dream-like, and, I found it to be very tranquil and calming. The puzzles sometimes make you think outside the box, which is also nice. As I stated before, the soundtrack is absolutely gorgeous. There are a lot of soothing ambient tracks in there, but, there are also some opera arias as well as the Moonlight Sonata, for example. The music fits the environments very well. Every level is set in a new environment and the puzzles get harder the more you delve into the game. I absolutely love this because it keeps things challenging and mind bending. You may find yourself getting frustrated because you feel "stuck" in a portion of the game, but, that didn't stop me from enjoying it one bit. So, if you are the type of person who loves surrealism, avant garde and outside of the box things, philosophy, metaphysics, and abstract art, then you will no doubt appreciate the beauty of this game.
 
LunaFortuna

√âvaluation publi√©e le 31 d√©cembre 2015
Rememored is a very brief, yet amazing, dreamlike experience.
There¬¥'s little in terms of gameplay, but the whole experience feels like a psychedelic dream, even if mostly black and white.

You are led into an exploration adventure inside an illogical, yet magical world and the atmosphere, mixed with the incredibly good music, engages the player on a sub-concious level.
Each small level you end up in you're constantly willing to go on exploring, just to experience the next amazing set piece the developers have in store for you.

Highly recommended if you like experimental videogames.
If you like gameplay-heavy games stay away (the game only asks to navigate the environments and do some very basic platforming).

A Surreal Exploration Adventure Game
Vid√©o YouTube‚Ñ¢: Rememoried || Surreal Exploration Adventure Game 
Vues : 131
#rememoried http://store.steampowered.com/app/368450/ + Very unique and interesting levels/environments that tries to break through the realm of imagination + A interesting game mechanic where the...

+ Very unique and interesting levels/environments that tries to break through the realm of imagination
+ A interesting game mechanic where the level will literally change every time you look away except for what you are standing on.
+ Relaxing soundtrack

- Very limited amounts of color, mostly black and white
- This game made me nauseous as you are constantly required to either spin in circles or look down, and when you look back up parts of the level changes. Mix that with some extremely bright white lights and random screen tearing and you may get a headache.
- The level where you are jumping on cloud to try to get to the top ladder is absolutely horrendous...not only do you have no idea where or what to do the platforming can be so "iffy" at times causing you to miss jumps that look in your reach.
- Most levels do not tell you what or where to go so you really need to use a guide to make any sort of progress


Even though I felt nauseating at times, the game gives a unique experience and certainly worthy to try out.
 
GamingTaylor

A great idea which is tarnished by simply unplayable mechanics which are the exact opposite of fun. Tried to like this, but there is no way I can truthfully recommend this highly experimental and volatile title to anyone under any circumstances. There's simply no way.

The whole gameplay revolves around having to figure out how to break out of the "forgetting loop" of each level. While sometimes clever, the solutions are highly unintuitive and even after having figured out the mechanic of the level, it will still take forever to actually execute the solution.

Play absolutely uninspired and tedious. Zero fun.

√âvaluation publi√©e le 16 d√©cembre 2017
An absolute gem, this game deserves far more praise than it's getting. It truly is nothing like anything you've played before.
And it's not just an "arty" game. The gameplay is pretty damn solid. Every single level is bizarrely straightforward though it somehow manages to appear completely obtuse on first glance (with the exception of the last one, that one had me stumped for probably the guts of an hour, the trick is to look for the bed ), and can be figured out through trial and error and reducing the level down to what stands out. And kudos to the developer for leaving that trail of logic to follow through the kaleidoscopic surrealism. The main crux of the game is that everything is constantly in flux when you look away, or depending on how you look at it, or from what direction, etc. Now while a lot of the levels do boil down to "find the exit, find the stepping stones to get through, and rotate your way through", there are quiet a number of truly ingenious ones that break with this formula entirely.
The game by and large seems quite bugfree at this stage, with the one exception where after a failed a level a couple of times I restarted at the start of the previous level instead of that level for some reason.
A truly unique surrealist experience that you absolutely have to play!
 
johntohill

√âvaluation publi√©e le 4 novembre 2015
We're knee-deep in "walking simulator" here - add "crazy abstract world" and "zero clues what's going on" and finally a few "rememoried.exe has stopped responding" dialog boxes for good measure!!

The dialogue is twaddle - it sounds like the stuff precocious 11-year-olds write in their poetry books whilst thinking they're being 'deep'.

I generally like games which create abstract worlds and manipulate them in interesting ways, but when you can't tell the difference between a gameplay element and the game crashiing, you've got a bit of an issue!

Truth is there's not a lot going-on here - there is some "finding things" and some "turning around" and a bit of "jumping on platforms" (sometimes near-invisible ones) but mostly the game plays the "wow, aren't I deep and trippy" car - well, until it plays the "I just crashed" card...

I'd steer clear of this - watch a video of it if you like the idea and save yourself the pain behind the eyes...
 
shrewdlogarithm

If you ever did acid without parental supervision then you will probably enjoy most of this game. If your experience with acid lead you to hypertension and illogical thought process relative to your surroundings then you will probably enjoy most of the game. If you ever believed that acid would transform you to a better understanding about irrelevant things in life then this game is most likely for you. If acid made you want to solve difficult and complex enigmas then I would say this game is not for you. This game wraps itself in a cloth of obscurity with obvious underwear beneath. 6/10.

Beautiful and interesting, for a while. I just wish that the people who make games with no guidance would understand that when you expect the player to do a certain thing, you have to make a way for the player to do that thing. Sure, get artsty, lose narrative, lose the normal conventions of gameplay. But the program expects the player to do something, and if you give the player no way to understand what they are to do, you just create pointless frustration.

There's enough frustration in life. I don't want to pay money to experience more.

Well what can I say. Another negative review and other people have said it all already. What is it with small scale indie devs that they just flat out refuse to do playable mechanics that make for enjoyable gameplay. Especially the gameplay that is supposed to be relaxing, like a casual stroll. Imho, the "forgetting" part is the game's blessing and a curse. I got bored after roughly 20 minutes on 2nd level with black and white boulders. You're supposed to advance further up and whenever you turn away from the rocks close to you the path changes. That was really annoying as you just keep jumping around in circles. Plus the GLARE!!! From all the glistening white and the particle fx. It is pretty if it's very short, but if entire level design is based on it then it grows on you rather quickly. Even NaissanceE, the short-lived let down that it was (i blame the ending), did the whole monochrome/sepia colour scheme a whole lot better.Also, the dialogue seemed weird and out of place. There's no controls for volume. You want to ship finished product to Steam, gog or whatever whatever platform at least playtest your stuff plenty. A sore, sore disappointment. I'll just go and replay Manifold Garden all over again I guess.

√âvaluation publi√©e le 2 novembre 2016
TL; DR: Very imaginative game environment, let down by a frustrating, underdeveloped game.

The joy of playing this game comes from exploring the gameworld: I found it a pleasantly disorienting experience. On the flipside, I didn't enjoy performing the actual tasks that represent the core gaming experience; you are thrown into the game with no clue as to what to do, and progression depends almost entirely on trial and error. I garnered no satisfaction from discovering the "solutions" because it was entirely a function of luck. Argh! Not my bag.

The game uses an interesting mechanic where environment changes as you look back and forth, but the designers didn't use it in a creative or entertaining way.

The gameworld is unique and curious enough to enjoy exploring for a short period (c. 1-2 hours), but the gameplay is tiresome and annoying - rather like searching for your keys in the dark.

Worth getting on sale just to enjoy the wonderfully surreal gameworld.

 
Seng Tsan

√âvaluation publi√©e le 30 juillet 2018
First person platformer with a focus on visuals held back by its own design.

While it indeed offered interesting sights during my brief stay, I gave up on the third level/puzzle I was presented with because both the first and the third revolved around not looking at platforms (unmoving when looked upon) and waiting, hoping that they would be aligned when turning around, allowing you to proceed toward the goal.
The huge size of the third level/puzzle discouraged me from pushing on after an unfortunate fall close to its ending, caused mostly by my impatience but also by the poor depth perception that plagues first person platforming and is made even worse by the stark and minimalistic aesthetic; upon death, I respawned at the very bottom and beginning of the stage after a grueling 15 minutes climb.
In fear the game would try and waste my time for several more levels similar to those, I gave up.

It might be your cup of tea, but it certainly wasn't mine.

This game has some very distinct strengths and weaknesses, which makes me a bit hesitant to recommend it. I go into more detail in my full written review[feedmepixels.com] (Minor puzzle spoilers, but I personally think you'd thank me). The video at the top of the page illustrates some of my problems with the platforming.

Pros:

-Good sound design
-Great visuals
-Beautiful, abstract aesthetic

‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•:

-Repetitive, RNG dependent mechanic that is present through the whole game
-Difficult to discern if some platforms would take you where you want to go or take you further away
-Sometimes arbitrary, impossible to guess objectives. Sometimes just tripping over the thing you need is the only way to proceed.

Overall, I personally feel the ‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô• outweigh the pros since your enjoyment of one is almost completely reliant on the other.

√âvaluation publi√©e le 13 d√©cembre 2015
OK, so I finished the game (rather, I finished the last level - you will see what I mean, if you play it) and I don't know how I did it. You see, I tried that level many times with no avail. But just now, I went at it again and finished it in 30 seconds. I would like to load it up again and see how I did it, but this game has no such options.
If you think this situation is weird, well, you've seen nothing yet. This game has some of the most creative and bizarre walking (or, should I say, finding) levels you are ever likely to see. The one with the segmented world falling apart is simply breathtaking, although really short. These walking levels are intertwined with some of the most irritating and psychotic platforming sections found in gaming.
I'd say this game fits in the same category as works of art like Naissancee and Mind: Path to Thalmus, yet is not like those games in any regard, if that makes sense.
Not for everyone, but a milestone nevertheless.

Non recommand√©
2.1 h en tout
√âvaluation publi√©e le 18 novembre 2019
Produit rembours√©

Other people have summed up the problems with this game pretty well. It's beautiful, has great soundtrack and atmosphere, and I actually don't mind the controls in the context of the game. But this game really shoots itself in the foot. I love casual puzzle platformers with great ambiance. Gris is my baseline for what a good version of this game would look like. Rememoried seems to be true woke (as opposed to some of the fake woke sorts of personal emotional quest games out there). That is to say that it seems to have a real thoughtful point it is trying to get across, rather than being some stereotypical message wrapped up in the container of a platformer. However, it totally fails to offer compelling gameplay. The way you solve the puzzles (the rememoried mechanic) seems completely random. On the third level you have to basically spin in circles over and over until you get the right platforms to keep jumping. There's no figuring out how to use it to get better at solving puzzles. It feels like this game was going for a dreamy and intangible approach to the gameplay, where the mechanics are directly tied in with your movement. Instead they landed more on vague puzzle platformer that doesn't hold your hand in all the wrong ways. People have said it before, but the "puzzles" really do make no sense. Which might seem a little strange to say about puzzles, because generally that's the point, but if you compare this game to something like Antichamber, there is really a night and day difference. One game clearly lines out different puzzles which you approach and solve through trial and error, getting feedback about each attempt until the logic of each stage clicks. There's not really a logic to what you're supposed to do. It doesn't feel so much like you progress by learning to operate within the rules of the game, so much as the rules of the game are arbitrary to intentionally make things difficult. And this means there's not an increase in logical difficulty, so much as an increase in vagueness between levels which leaves you feeling less like you're getting better, and more like you're just an idiot for not understanding what is going on when the narrator says something vague about dreams and memories.
 
Hexophile

BEWILDERING WONDER!

One of the most controversial and original games of the last years.

Poetry is in the air in "Rememoried", this game will mess with your mind, it will confuse you and will also inspire you to take your life in a more magic way!

The gameplay is an enigma itself, basic controls, but understanding what you have to do is the most difficult thing and this will keep you busy, very busy! The graphic is simply ASTONISHING, sweet to see and full of colors and emotions.

Playing this will make you feel as when you wake up from a dream and you don't understand what just happened.

Go for it, try this oniric videogame and play it. It is not a game, it is a journey.

Videogame News, Indie Score: 9 | SUPER RECOMMENDED

√âvaluation publi√©e le 16 novembre 2015
I'm a pretty big fan of this sort of game but I can't recommend this one.

The graphics are OK in general and some scenes look quite good but you will spend most of your time just wandering around looking for a random object, or continaully spinning around to make platforms spawn in the right place (they appear or disapear while not looking). Those mechanics are reused many times and it just makes for a tedious experience overall.

Then there is the dialogue which is essentially nonsense. It sounds like they think it's deep but you just can't take it seriously with comments like "Space is dogma. Dogma is logic" or "Space and time are just definitions".

When you do finish a level it just fades into the next one, often before you actually reach the thing you're trying to get to. It leaves you without any real sense of achievement.

So while I wanted to like this game, I just couldn't. But, I do see potential in the developers, perhaps they will learn from their mistakes and make somethimg more worthwhile for their next game.
 
Astiolo

Rememoried is a surrealistic exploration platforming/puzzle game with great visual design. Most levels involve searching for an exit while finding the right path or rotating your way through correctly. Each level is vastly different and gives no clues on how to solve it which may be a negative for some people. Several platforming sections are frustrating but can be completed with patience. The game took me less than 3 hours to complete but I would go back to explore the surreal environments again. [7/10]

I‚Äòll start with exploration aspect of the game ‚Äì this part could work very well...if it wasnt for two things. 1) Since there is no story, the only reason why somebody would explore is to see sureal stuff and listen to nice music (I‚Äòll go over that later) , unfortunately levels arent that big and if you cross the line where level should end, you‚Äòll die (or return to start of the level) and once you explore the level, you‚Äòll be trying to proceed to next one, but thats mostly frustrating, since the game tells you nothing about what are you supposed to do and you're left on your own to figure out games logic to proceed to next level. its mostly finding somethings, but even with that its still sometimes like trying to find a needle in a haystack, except you're not told that you suppose to find a needle but that you probably need to find something

2)voices ‚Äì in begining of the level, you‚Äòll hear the voices often saying some ‚Äò‚Äòartsy‚Äò‚Äò stuff and by ‚Äò‚Äòartsy‚Äò‚Äò i mean nonsensical things that are supposed to be deep, but ends up being uninteresting and annoying.. Adding a salt into an injury, voices have echoey , spacey like sound that will drive normal person insane and you‚Äòll die a lot (mostly in platforming sections and sections where are some flying small flames) so you are going to hear them a lot.The game would be better of without those voices,with them the game just looks more pretentious.

at last lets discus puzzle/platforming parts ‚Äì They are awful ‚Äì its usually try to get to that point while jump on rocks or platforms, but then you come to a point where you cant jump on other platform since its too far away...thats where you discover mechanic of forgetting ‚Äì everytime you look away and look back again, platforms will be on different places ‚Äì This is maybe good idea on paper, but in its execution its just annoying ‚Äì to move platform thats far away from you have to look away and back to move it,but where the platform will place itself is completely random, so you‚Äòll end up doing it multiple times.Sometimes it works on a first attempt, most of the time it doesnt.

Visuals/music ‚Äì visuals and music are Highlights of this game.Visuals are beautifull.They are spacey ,very dream - like and overall relaxing (even though the game is sometimes so frustrating and tiresome because of puzzles, you would be less frustrated by figuring out silent hill 3 shakespear puzzle on the highest difficulty in japanese). Music is also great ‚Äì subtle,minimalistic and melancholic with bits of classical music.These two things go hand with hand (aside one level where the Moonlight sonata starts to play and it feels a bit out of place)

pros :
- beautifull visuals and music
-well........there were like 1-2 levels that were cool to explore

‚ô•‚ô•‚ô•‚ô• :
- awful puzzle/platforming section
- frustrating sureal puzzles wiithout clues
- pointles and annoying voices
- no story (or atleast one thats explained in a game and not wikipedia)
- annoying ,,forgeting'' mechanic

verdict - I am sure devs had a good intentions and ideas, but the final product is just pretentious and tiresome mess I'll admit that its nice looking and pretty sounding mess, but thats pretty much it.I cant reccomend this game to adventure - exploring fans, because of shi**y platforming and i cant reccomend this to puzzle/platforming crowd, because of shi**y platforming and frustrating level proceeding.Those who like surealism and have strong patience will maybe find some enjoyment out of it, but even then the game is just not good.
4/10
 
Willy Schmiprdel

I've only played the first 40 or 50 minutes of the game so far but so far so good! The game's visuals are surreal and interesting, the voice acting and music are pleasant and professional, and it features a really interesting "forgetting" mechanic, where objects and platforms change, disappear, and materialize simply through looking around.
Vid√©o YouTube‚Ñ¢: The First 45 Minutes of Rememoried: Let's Play (Puzzle adventure, indie game, and gameplay) 
Vues : 7,185
The First 45 Minutes of Rememoried: Let's Play (Puzzle adventure, indie game, and gameplay) Rememoried is a surreal adventure puzzle indie game, and in this video we'll explore some of the game's...

The gameplay is simple, but so far the puzzles are quite unique in it's design. It's certainly one of the more interesting "walking simulator" I've played. It actually makes looking around and wandering very much an active mechanic which has some pretty interesting results.

The video above is the my first 45 minutes of gameplay of Remomoried. It's not a critical analysis, but it does show honest gameplay and my first time reactions to it for those who might be curious.

√âvaluation publi√©e le 13 septembre 2015
Very enjoyable game. There used to be one really annoying thing that after you made a mistake you had to play the previous level again, but that's fixed now, you can kill yourself as many times as you like and start the same level again without penalties, much more fun that way :)

Surreal atmosphere, things change when you are not looking at them, great graphics. I don't like reverb in the vocals that much, but you don't have to re-play previous levels so I can live with that. If you like Dear Esther, this is definitely a game for you. If you only play FPS, don't even bother. Have fun!

√âvaluation publi√©e le 31 d√©cembre 2016
This game comes across as an art piece, but it is not meant to be fun. The game is frustrating and confusing at times in ways which go against conventional game design. The main mechanic is that things change when you are not looking, but it seems random as to whether you'll get something useful or not.

On one particular puzzle with a windmill, the mechanic got worse though... jumping between platforms and turning around to make new ones appear would sometimes make the one you were already standing on disappear and drop you. The amount of jumping that it would require to do it without this was already significant, so this just added to the frustration.

The fact that the game doesn't "end" made things all the worse, as it just loops you back to the start after completing 20-something levels with no indication that you've actually finished...

I got this for 90% off and even then i feel this isn't worth the time.
 
kazenone

It is weird.

Vid√©o YouTube‚Ñ¢: Rememoried Gameplay - Quicky Look 
Vues : 422
Rememoried gameplay and first impressions of Rememoried. This is a weird one. Thanks for watching/liking/subscribing!!! It is appreciated.


The first level is quite bad at telling you what you should be doing but other then that I can't find other faults from the game.

Oh wait yes I can. The default controls for jumping are set to the left/right mouse buttons?
That's just messed up.
Thankfully though you can change it from the config menu.

Graphically it looks pretty even on the lower graphics settings.

The settings themselves are just... Weird as I said before and that in my opinion is the best thing about this game.
Floating eyeballs, stars, suprising amount of comfy chairs and other bizarre things await you.

Based on the first 4 levels, it seem that one level would take about 10 to 15 minutes to beat, maybe less so and with the 20 in game levels it can be a short game so take that into account when purchasing.

Here's a gameplay video of the first few levels if you would like to check it out!

√âvaluation publi√©e le 16 septembre 2016
TLDR:
Poor platforming with vague goals, nausea-inducing gameplay. Stay away from this one.

Review:
I really didn't enjoy this game at all... and I for the most part enjoy "artsy" games... The gameplay in this game revolves around you for the most part needing to jump on platforms, and when you don't have a way forward you have to look away and then back to see the platforms have changed. You have to do this, back and forth until you get a platform you can walk/jump to.

As someone who gets dizzy by turning around in circles very easily in real life, this was a horrible experience for me. I got really nauseous by the time I completed the game after 2.2 hours. I had to use a guide as well, since what you had to do to progress often was so ambiguous..

And first person platforming is never especially good, and this one is especially bad in this regard.
I multiple times fell to the bottom of a section and had to redo the whole ting again, just because a platform had spawned above my head and I crashed into it while trying to jump to another platform.

I can respect that some people really like this sort of game, it's just not my cup of tea.

My grade: 3/10
 
Vlash

√âvaluation publi√©e le 30 novembre 2016
Basing on merely first impressions, I must discard this game. Even though its theme is praiseworthy, the execution paradoxically falls short, perhaps due to baroque eyesore-causing overabundance, with too little content. Maybe I am just more keen on minimalism, that is why the opinion. This way or the other, agreeing with what has already been said among the reviews: good art, poor play. Work misplacement. By definition I would categorize it as a first person view exploration-platformer, set within three dimentional surrealistic environment. To call it a puzzle game is a major confusion. While the modest exploration aspect could be rated up, the platforming is an issue. The game has some annoyances founded as its core mechanics, that will make the proceeding unnecessarily difficult, even chaotic. Furthermore, if to think about it, the graphical design is stubborn at times as well.

√âvaluation publi√©e le 7 novembre 2019
It's a first-person puzzle game, in which you are exploring a dream-world, full of surealism and fleeting thoughts. There's no plot, per se, but in each vingette you are searching for a seemingly out-of-reach goal. Most of the time the path is non-fixed, and every time you turn back around the landscape and pieces have changed--both to your frustration and to your advantage as a gameplay mechanic. As you can see, the art design is mostly black and white with a few splashes of colors that flicker in and out. It's really quite beautiful.
 
*blink*blink*

If you want a silky-smooth meditative experience with a few gentle puzzles thrown in, absolutely get Rememoried. This is the videogame equivalent of walking through a zen garden. It's easy enough that you can "beat it" on autopilot while being entranced by the visuals and music. I've played it a lot and personally, I find it helps with anxiety.

2.2 h en tout
√âvaluation publi√©e le 18 octobre 2016
It's a solid exploration/puzzle game that goes for a dreamlike feel and nails it really well with the Forgetting mechanic, doing a great job of mimicking how things in dreams can change and move just because you look away from them for a moment. Likewise, both the soundtrack and visuals help immerse you in the dream-world, though I will say that the random glitchy camera effects were a bit off-putting.

A few of the more platformey levels are rough around the edges, as you'll often need to Forget the area around you multiple times until the platforms end up in locations you can actually jump to, but the more puzzle-oriented levels are where the game really shines, with a number of puzzles making very clever use of the Forgetting mechanics.

If there was a story, it was so far into existential 2deep4u territory that it completely flew over my head. The dialogue seemed to be talking about varying aspects of existence and reality but there was no real cohesion to it (funnily fitting as that's how dialogue can often be in dreams).

Overall, it reminded me of both Antichamber and LSD: Dream Emulator, and as far as 2-hour atmospheric quickie games go it's quite the enjoyable experience.
 
arsenicBumpnip
